<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ba623989-14fb-46f7-98ba-c4f30984c679'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

  <b></b>
</p><p> Darkness, air, water, and sky will come together...   </p><p> The wild cats of the forest have lived in peace and harmony for many moons but a doom that will change everything is coming. Strange messages from their warrior ancestors speak of terrifying new prophecies, danger, and a mysterious destiny. </p> <p> All the signs point to young warrior Brambleclaw as the cat with the fate of the forest in his paws. But why would the son of wicked cat Tigerstar be chosen to be a hero? And who are the other cats mentioned in the prophecy? All Brambleclaw knows for sure is that the strength and courage of the greatest warriors will be needed now, as the quest to save the Clans begins. </p> <b></b><p> ...and shake the forest to its roots.  </p></span>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/80574098-jojo">Jojo</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I don't think 7-year-olds would be mature enough to read the books. The first time I actually took a quick glance into the book was when i was 8, and <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I don't think 7-year-olds would be mature enough to read the books. The first time I actually took a quick glance into the book was when i was 8, and I found it hard to understand the vocabulary, and the type of "style" in which I mean the 'paws, 'stars, and 'kits. I also think that they wouldn't understand that the series isn't just some fun fantasy. It also includes death and violence, which I don't quite think is allowed to be shown to small kids.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

But in this one absolutely NOTHING HAPPENED!<br />It was just like..<br />(sing to the tune of "Follow the Leader")<br />"WE'RE GOING ON A JOURNEY,A JOURNEY,A JOURNEY<br />WE'RE GOING ON A JOURNEY, OR ELSE OUR CLANS WILL DIE!"<br />and even thought they all new the clans were in trouble, the six cats on the journey were in no apparent hurry to get home.<br /><br />Well ok, something did happen.<br />They found midnight.<br />thats it...:)<br /><br />My favorite character in this book was Squirrelpaw. She kinda reminded me of the annoying orange.<br />"HEY HEY BRAMBLECLAW(apple)! HEY BRAMBLECLAW(apple) HEY!!"<br />"WHAT,SQUIRRELPAW(orange), WHAT?!"<br />"BADGER(knife)!"<br />"AHH!!!!!!!!!!!!"<br />(sounds familiar?)<br />Not to mention how much Crowpaw reminded me of midget apple.<br />sorry. i watch WAAAAAAYYY too much youtube.<br />:)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17133018009370010468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_621459542" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621459542" />
    <a title="haley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20582304-haley"><img alt="haley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546379722p2/20582304.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/621459542?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="haley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="haley" href="/user/show/20582304-haley">haley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20582304-haley?shelf=erin-hunter-books">erin-hunter-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20582304-haley?shelf=amazing">amazing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20582304-haley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621459542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16110621786934364735">Alrighty! I finally re-read all the New Prophecy books, with the exception of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/296942.Moonrise__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___2_' title='Moonrise (Warriors The New Prophecy, #2) by Erin Hunter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Moonrise</a> as I don't own a copy and was too lazy to go to the library.<br/>I'm currently re-reading the entire series so I can write new, updated reviews.<br/><br/>So note that this review is for ALL of the New Prophecy books (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/273511.Midnight__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___1_' title='Midnight (Warriors The New Prophecy, #1) by Erin Hunter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Midnight</a>-<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/197459.Sunset__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___6_' title='Sunset (Warriors The New Prophecy, #6) by Erin Hunter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sunset</a>). Also, another thing. Names change throughout the series as the cats grow up (a sort of Rite of Passage). For the sake of simplicity, I will refer to characters with the names they have in the f</span>
  <span id="freeText16110621786934364735" style="display:none">Alrighty! I finally re-read all the New Prophecy books, with the exception of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/296942.Moonrise__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___2_" title="Moonrise (Warriors The New Prophecy, #2) by Erin Hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Moonrise</a> as I don't own a copy and was too lazy to go to the library.<br />I'm currently re-reading the entire series so I can write new, updated reviews.<br /><br />So note that this review is for ALL of the New Prophecy books (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/273511.Midnight__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___1_" title="Midnight (Warriors The New Prophecy, #1) by Erin Hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight</a>-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/197459.Sunset__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___6_" title="Sunset (Warriors The New Prophecy, #6) by Erin Hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Sunset</a>). Also, another thing. Names change throughout the series as the cats grow up (a sort of Rite of Passage). For the sake of simplicity, I will refer to characters with the names they have in the first book. So Squirrelpaw/Squirrelflight will be Squirrelpaw.<br /><br />Overall, the six books that make up the Warriors: New Prophecy sub-series are excellent. They definitely don't beat the original six, but certainly are worthy of being part of the Warriors saga.<br /><br />What I liked:<br />1. Brambleclaw. Throughout all the New Prophecy books, I always felt that I could sympathize with him. He's got a lot of responsibility for someone his age (he's a cat so I'm not certain of his age. But I'm guessing that if he was human, he'd be 17-18 years old). But he handles it well. He has a good soul but he also struggles with the temptation of being like his power-hungry father, Tigerclaw. And this makes him more complex as a character. He makes mistakes, but learns from them too. The whole time I felt all his emotions. I was angry when something bad happened to him, I cheered when he was happy and overall, I just feel like he's a character one can really cheer for and support.<br /><br />2. Although originally, I <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ hated the change of setting because I was feeling nostalgic and sad that the home the Clans had lived in for generations upon generations was destroyed  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, now I appreciate it. The storyline would have grown boring without it.<br /><br />3. The plot-line throughout the whole sub-series is interesting. It doesn't seem contrived, it doesn't seem unrealistic. Although the later three books (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/273512.Starlight__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___4_" title="Starlight (Warriors The New Prophecy, #4) by Erin Hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Starlight</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/252938.Twilight__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___5_" title="Twilight (Warriors The New Prophecy, #5) by Erin Hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/197459.Sunset__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___6_" title="Sunset (Warriors The New Prophecy, #6) by Erin Hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Sunset</a>) are about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the politics of the Clans settling into their new home  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> (which I actually found fascinating but perhaps not everyone will), the first three books (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/273511.Midnight__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___1_" title="Midnight (Warriors The New Prophecy, #1) by Erin Hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/296942.Moonrise__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___2_" title="Moonrise (Warriors The New Prophecy, #2) by Erin Hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Moonrise</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/111021.Dawn__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___3_" title="Dawn (Warriors The New Prophecy, #3) by Erin Hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Dawn</a>) are full of action and adventure.<br /><br />Although I am a huge fan of the Warriors saga overall, I can see its faults and don't love everything about it. Here's what I had problems with in the New Prophecy books:<br />1. Insta-love. Holy crap, the Erins do love their forbidden romances. Yellowfang and Raggedstar. Bluestar and Oakheart. Graystripe and Silverstream. Tigerheart and Dovewing (in the Omen of the Stars books). In the New Prophecy books, we have <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Leafpaw and Crowpaw  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I just don't see the attraction. She is a sweet, if naive at times, little thing while he is just so bitter. He's not really annoying (although I hated him at first), but he's just so different from her I don't see how it ever happened. Not to mention he was in love with another cat first.<br /><br />2. A love triangle. These books have insta-love AND a love triangle, both of which I hate? And it still got four stars? How?? Because I love the Warriors saga too dang much. These things only apply to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/252938.Twilight__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___5_" title="Twilight (Warriors The New Prophecy, #5) by Erin Hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/197459.Sunset__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___6_" title="Sunset (Warriors The New Prophecy, #6) by Erin Hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Sunset</a> anyways. Anyway, the love triangle is fought over a female character that I hate so I have to wonder how she got two intelligent and decent guy cats fighting for her. Rejection also turns one cat into an ass, and why, why, why did that have to happen? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Ashfur was a decent cat, so I don't understand how he could have gone from such a sweetie to a complete asshole??  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />3. Squirrelpaw. This little bitch needs a slap. And a hard one. So at first, she was only a minor nuisance. Course I will claw- geez, I'm talking like the warriors now- anyone who disagrees with my Brambleclaw, who I have a sort of crush on (I know, it's sort of messed up cause he's a cat). So maybe that's why I didn't like her, because she was always picking fights with Brambleclaw. But on the journey, she proves her worth with her strength, her loyalty and her bravery. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/111021.Dawn__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___3_" title="Dawn (Warriors The New Prophecy, #3) by Erin Hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Dawn</a>, I definitely respected her a bit, just a bit more.<br />Then <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/273512.Starlight__Warriors_The_New_Prophecy___4_" title="Starlight (Warriors The New Prophecy, #4) by Erin Hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Starlight</a> happened. And she got extremely possessive over Brambleclaw, which made me start to hate her. You see, Squirrelpaw was convinced that Hawkfrost, who is Brambleclaw's half-brother, cannot be trusted and he's just like their evil dad Tigerclaw. Even though there's absolutely no evidence for this except for her and her sister Leafpaw's gut feelings. Squirrelpaw constantly judges Hawkfrost. Brambleclaw, who is interested in having a relationship with his kin, also faces Squirrelpaw's judgement and anger because she feels that because Hawkfrost is untrustworthy, then Brambleclaw is untrustworthy too just because he spends time with Hawkfrost (I know, it's a lot of angst and drama).And it pissed me off beacuse hey, Squirrelpaw, you have no right ot tell him who he can and cannot be friends with. Brambleclaw is an adult and can take care of himself. What irks me even more was that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ in the end, Squirrelpaw was actually right and Hawkfrost turned out to be evil  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. And then Brambleclaw just goes crawling back to her. I just feel he deserves more, someone better than her. <br /><br />And that's really it. Trust me, the good does outweigh the bad, so I do highly recommend this for Warriors fans. You may not be bothered by what bothered me. Overall an excellent series of books. Happy reading!<br /><br />***************************************************************************************************************************************************<br />Because there are so MANY books in the Warriors saga, here is the list (in order) of all the books in the main arc. This does not include the Dawn of the Clans books, or the Super Editions (which can be read independently of the main books.<br />Also, please note that you can stop reading after the sixth book in each sub-series and you won't miss anything<br />Order of Books: <br /><b>(Warriors)</b><br />Warriors 1: Into the Wild<br />Warriors 2: Fire and Ice<br />Warriors 3: Forest of Secrets <br />Warriors 4: Rising Storm<br />Warriors 5: A Dangerous Path<br />Warriors 6: The Darkest Hour<br /><b>(Warriors: New Prophecy) </b><br />Warriors: New Prophecy 1: Midnight<br />Warriors: New Prophecy 2: Moonrise<br />Warriors: New Prophecy 3: Dawn<br />Warriors: New Prophecy 4: Starlight<br />Warriors: New Prophecy 5: Twilight<br />Warriors: New Prophecy 6: Sunset<br /><b>(Warriors: Power of Three)</b><br />Warriors: Power of Three 1: The Sight<br />Warriors: Power of Three 2: Dark River<br />Warriors: Power of Three 3: Outcast<br />Warriors: Power of Three 4: Eclipse<br />Warriors: Power of Three 5: Long Shadows<br />Warriors: Power of Three 6: Sunrise<br /><b>(Warriors: Omen of the Stars) </b><br />Warriors: Omen of the Stars 1: The Fourth Apprentice<br />Warriors: Omen of the Stars 2: Fading Echoes<br />Warriors: Omen of the Stars 3: Night whispers<br />Warriors: Omen of the Stars 4: Sign of the Moon<br />Warriors: Omen of the Stars 5: The Forgotten Warrior<br />Warriors: Omen of the Stars 6: The Last Hope<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16110621786934364735" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_402593063" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/402593063" />
    <a title="Ariel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6563683-ariel"><img alt="Ariel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567821958p2/6563683.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/402593063?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ariel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ariel" href="/user/show/6563683-ariel">Ariel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer402593063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5215339404609827555">Re-reading this reminds me why this is my least favorite of the Warriors series.<br/><br/>I hate Squirrelpaw. If there were at least some legitimate reason why she was a jerk the whole time then I could at least tolerate her, but there is absolutely no reason for her behavior. I'm sorry if I can't relate or sympathize with a character who yells at everyone for no reason, has no respect for anyone, constantly talks backs, and gets herself into dangerous situations after being warned and then acts like it's</span>
  <span id="freeText5215339404609827555" style="display:none">Re-reading this reminds me why this is my least favorite of the Warriors series.<br /><br />I hate Squirrelpaw. If there were at least some legitimate reason why she was a jerk the whole time then I could at least tolerate her, but there is absolutely no reason for her behavior. I'm sorry if I can't relate or sympathize with a character who yells at everyone for no reason, has no respect for anyone, constantly talks backs, and gets herself into dangerous situations after being warned and then acts like it's their fault. There is no way I could ever root for a character like that. What makes it worse is that I feel as the author wants me to think what a great character she is and how wonderful and brave and strong she is... nope.<br /><br />Then there's the whole traveling aspect of the book. The Erins aren't really good at writing them. They kind of drag. I could easily skim them and not miss much of anything. And considering that it takes up the vast majority of the book there really isn't much to actually read.<br /><br />I'm determined to re-read the rest of these books though. It's just going to be a struggle for the next few of them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5215339404609827555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10952326523379959867">Midnight (Warriors: The New Prophecy, #1) by Erin Hunter (Pages: 3 or 400.)<br/><br/><br/>I loved this book because this time the main character wasn't Firestar, it happened to have 2 main characters!   <span id="freeText10952326523379959867" style="display:none">Midnight (Warriors: The New Prophecy, #1) by Erin Hunter (Pages: 3 or 400.)<br /><br /><br />I loved this book because this time the main character wasn't Firestar, it happened to have 2 main characters! The 2 main characters this time are Brambeclaw and a new medicine cat apprentice (AKA: Firestars daughter) Leafpaw. Leafpaw is having visions of her sister, Squirrelpaw and what she faces while Brambleclaw got a new prophecy: Darkness, Air, Water, And sky will shake the forest to its roots. Nobody knows what it means (Well, Brambleclaw doesn't since he didn't tell anybody at all about this dream.)<br />Also, atleast 4 cats from each clan got a dream. These cats are: Brambleclaw, his sister: Tawnypaw, Crowpaw, and Feathertail. They each got a dream from old starclan members that there was danger coming. (But Firestars other daughter, Squirrelpaw and another Riverclan warrior, Stormfur, came for extra protection on a long journey to a place that is very dangerous.) The 6 cats are all going on an adventure to a sun-drown-place, when the sun goes down, it is red and the water is salty and there is a huge cave with sharp teeth. Brambleclaw had a dream of this and he decided Starclan wanted them to go there. So now all 6 cats are going on an adventure to somewhere no forest cat has really been before!<br /><br />I believe everyone should read this book cause there is some events that nobody would of experienced in the first series: The prophecies begin.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer841694498" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14967961579546017128">I felt like this book was set to be a bit of a letdown; after the ending to the first Warriors series, I really don't see how anything could compare. This definitely felt like an introduction, but still kept some of the same aspects and situations as the first series so as not to scare long time readers. There are also more 'travel' scenes, reminiscent of all the camping that goes on in 'Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows'. You know they're all headed towards something, and you can't wait to g</span>
  <span id="freeText14967961579546017128" style="display:none">I felt like this book was set to be a bit of a letdown; after the ending to the first Warriors series, I really don't see how anything could compare. This definitely felt like an introduction, but still kept some of the same aspects and situations as the first series so as not to scare long time readers. There are also more 'travel' scenes, reminiscent of all the camping that goes on in 'Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows'. You know they're all headed towards something, and you can't wait to get there with them.<br /><br />I love the new characters, and the fleshing out of some old names. Firestar reads like Simba in the second Lion King movie, I've even got that song that plays when Kovu is chased from th pridelands stuck in my head now! -Deception, Disgrace, evil as clear as the scar on his faaaace!-<br /> <br />I am a fairly easy to please reader, and I don't really try books I know I'm not going to like (like that isn't obvious from my rating average) I don't mind reader filler scenes and introductions so long as there is action somewhere, and from this ending you can tell the series will pick up. I will be there to follow the journey, I know I have the next few books. Look out for new reviews is the coming days!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14967961579546017128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4015454199683927746">EPIC! Yeah, it's time to follow the next generation of warriors! This is the first book of the 2nd arc, The New Prophecy, WARRIORS. Several peaceful moons (6 months) have passed since the last book - The Darkest Hour. Lot's of exciting stuff happens and we learn a lot, as new characters come into this series. It may be strange to have new main characters at first but you quickly get to love them just as much as Firestar and Graystripe. The book alternated between different viewpoints which is go</span>
  <span id="freeText4015454199683927746" style="display:none">EPIC! Yeah, it's time to follow the next generation of warriors! This is the first book of the 2nd arc, The New Prophecy, WARRIORS. Several peaceful moons (6 months) have passed since the last book - The Darkest Hour. Lot's of exciting stuff happens and we learn a lot, as new characters come into this series. It may be strange to have new main characters at first but you quickly get to love them just as much as Firestar and Graystripe. The book alternated between different viewpoints which is good, as it propels the story forward and they always start at a different viewpoint when something really exciting happens. This means it's really hard to put the book down and makes it more enjoyable in my opinion. Full of thrilling suspence, gasps and overall a really enjoyable book. We follow The Chosen Cats from Thunderclan, Shadowcaln, Windclan and Riverclan on a JOURNEY.... Friendships are made, new places are discovered and new problems arise. AWESOME - :)</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3480370460?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joseph Fullbright" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joseph Fullbright" href="/user/show/112732488-joseph-fullbright">Joseph Fullbright</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112732488-joseph-fullbright?shelf=warriors">warriors</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3480370460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1050896099320441866">While relatively slow, this book seems like a perfect launchpad for the second arc in the Warriors series. It was so cool to see the four chosen cats from each clan come together and go on the journey to 'Midnight' without anyone else having a clue as to where they are. One of my favorite parts of this book was seeing the interaction between these new cats (Brambleclaw, Squirrelflight, Leafpaw, etc.) and the 'original' cats from the first arc (Firestar, Graystripe, Cinderpelt, etc.). It's almost</span>
  <span id="freeText1050896099320441866" style="display:none">While relatively slow, this book seems like a perfect launchpad for the second arc in the Warriors series. It was so cool to see the four chosen cats from each clan come together and go on the journey to 'Midnight' without anyone else having a clue as to where they are. One of my favorite parts of this book was seeing the interaction between these new cats (Brambleclaw, Squirrelflight, Leafpaw, etc.) and the 'original' cats from the first arc (Firestar, Graystripe, Cinderpelt, etc.). It's almost as if we somewhat grew up WITH those older cats.<br /><br />Not a spoiler, but I got chill bumps reading the prologue- seeing the respective cats of the past select the chosen four to go on the journey to save the Clans. You'll just have to read it to understand! Oh, and Ravenpaw's brief interaction with Brambleclaw on pages 94-95 was truly EPIC and heartwarming.<br /><br />I'm not a HUGE fan of the book switching and going back-and-forth between different cat's points of view, but that provided an alternative twist that was intriguing. Overall, it was awesome being introduced to the new generation of Warriors and following them on their journey. This book was so much fun and, as I mentioned earlier, did a GREAT job setting up the rest of the arc! I don't necessarily remember this second arc as much as the first, so I am greatly looking forward to re-reading it and seeing what happens next!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1050896099320441866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2739654524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14685695226369494605"><b>3.5/5</b><br/><br/>Okay, this one didn't <i>quite</i> have the magic that the first series held for me. But I still enjoyed stepping back into the world of the cat Clans just the same!<br/><br/>Compared to the first series, this book was rather slow. In fact, nothing really <i>happened</i>. There was a lot of talk about prophecy, a lot of traveling, and not much action. There were only a few scenes where the cats were in any danger. I think the bar was set too high by the last series, which delivered tons of action, harrowing danger</span>
  <span id="freeText14685695226369494605" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5</b><br /><br />Okay, this one didn't <i>quite</i> have the magic that the first series held for me. But I still enjoyed stepping back into the world of the cat Clans just the same!<br /><br />Compared to the first series, this book was rather slow. In fact, nothing really <i>happened</i>. There was a lot of talk about prophecy, a lot of traveling, and not much action. There were only a few scenes where the cats were in any danger. I think the bar was set too high by the last series, which delivered tons of action, harrowing danger, and heartbreak; this book had none of that. It felt like a very long prequel to set up the prophecy. I'm hoping the second book picks up a bit!<br /><br />I'm so happy that Brambleclaw turned out okay, despite his father. It was cool to read from his point of view, even though I do miss Firestar's POV a lot. (Side note: He and Sandstorm finally had kits! Squeeee!!!) I loved meeting Firestar's daughters, and love the connection they share together. Do I sense a possible romance brewing between Brambleclaw and Squirrelpaw?!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14685695226369494605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1128763952?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hunter K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hunter K" href="/user/show/33652418-hunter-k">Hunter K</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1128763952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8628150275248796831">Summary <br/>Warriors is a series that is very exciting and adventurous. This book is about how six cats go on a journey to find midnight. They meet Purdy, a kitty pet who makes him their guide on their journey. He tries to lead them in the direction of the sea but gets lost. Then when they’re in the up walkers territory they get ambushed by rats and Tawnypelt gets injured bad. <br/><br/>Main characters <br/>Tawnypelt- strong from shadow clan.<br/>Brambleclaw- big powerful tabby from thunder clan.<br/>Stormfur- gray graystri</span>
  <span id="freeText8628150275248796831" style="display:none">Summary <br />Warriors is a series that is very exciting and adventurous. This book is about how six cats go on a journey to find midnight. They meet Purdy, a kitty pet who makes him their guide on their journey. He tries to lead them in the direction of the sea but gets lost. Then when they’re in the up walkers territory they get ambushed by rats and Tawnypelt gets injured bad. <br /><br />Main characters <br />Tawnypelt- strong from shadow clan.<br />Brambleclaw- big powerful tabby from thunder clan.<br />Stormfur- gray graystripes son river clan.<br />Crowpaw-apprentice windclan.<br />Feathertail- sister of stormfur river clan.<br />Squirrelpaw- firestar’s daughter. Thunderclan.<br />Firestar- leader of thunderclan.<br />Leafpaw- sister of squirrelpaw medicine cat apprentice. Thunder clan.<br />Cinderpelt- medicine cat. Thunder clan.<br />Purdy- guide, kittypet, friend. Clanless.<br /><br />Setting<br />In the deep dark forest by mother mouth and by the deep blue sea by the harsh rocks that looks like teeth. By the sea is where the cats meet midnight. In the forest is where the clans are. The forest has high ridges and a river that runs threw three of the clans. <br />	<br />Conflict<br />The forest is being attacked by dirty nasty twolegs who don’t know about the clan cats. They have started fires. Let viscous dogs in who attacked them. Last they have taken cats.<br /><br />Resolve of conflict<br />The six cats are trying to get the clans to go away from the forest which is being demolished. The two legs were going to build a new thunder path right through the forest. That is why they have to leave. That is why Purdy is helping them. <br /><br />Opinion <br />I think it was a very interesting and exciting book. It had a lot of different views which I liked. It gets sad at times too. But in the end they survive<br /><br />Recommendation <br />I would recommend it to anyone who likes adventure and cats. Adventure because there always doing something. Cats because it’s about cats. And that’s who I would recommend it to.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17698548648408276700">The New Prophecy - and probably all the other series - isn't as good as the original, in my opinion. I still LOVE the books, but if I'm comparing them, the original is the best, and probably always will be. I still found this book really interesting and I really got into it in the second half. I love the balance between dialogue and description and that makes it good fr all ages. You really get to know most characters and really feel for them and know what they're feeling. I find it really easy </span>
  <span id="freeText17698548648408276700" style="display:none">The New Prophecy - and probably all the other series - isn't as good as the original, in my opinion. I still LOVE the books, but if I'm comparing them, the original is the best, and probably always will be. I still found this book really interesting and I really got into it in the second half. I love the balance between dialogue and description and that makes it good fr all ages. You really get to know most characters and really feel for them and know what they're feeling. I find it really easy to like/dislike certain characters, and that's something I like about books - character interaction with the reader. In this book we change out of Firestar's kind of perspective, which is nice after having a whole series with his perspective. It still centres around ThunderClan like the original series, but it's great to change perspective. Exciting book and I really loved it, just not the best compared to the original series books.<br /><br />For more information about this book and others, check out my YouTube channel: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/TheDougieowner">www.youtube.com/TheDougieowner</a></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3636672118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15501897749403248182"><b>1.6</b> :(<br/><br/><br/>This is the most hilarious novel I've ever read. <u>EVER.</u> Why? Because... ah... nothing happened, and most of the book was seriously stuff about them eating fish. Um... <i>okay</i>... I get you have to eat, cats, but... ¯\_(ツ)_/¯ You know what. Let's move on.<br/><br/>I was an incredibly stupid kid when I picked this up. I thought this was the first book - and it <i>was</i> a first book... except for the fact that it was <i>the first book of a spinoff</i>. Let us applaud the foolishness of me, people. *slow clap* Also, is </span>
  <span id="freeText15501897749403248182" style="display:none"><b>1.6</b> :(<br /><br /><br />This is the most hilarious novel I've ever read. <u>EVER.</u> Why? Because... ah... nothing happened, and most of the book was seriously stuff about them eating fish. Um... <i>okay</i>... I get you have to eat, cats, but... ¯\_(ツ)_/¯ You know what. Let's move on.<br /><br />I was an incredibly stupid kid when I picked this up. I thought this was the first book - and it <i>was</i> a first book... except for the fact that it was <i>the first book of a spinoff</i>. Let us applaud the foolishness of me, people. *slow clap* Also, is it just me or is it really, really ridiculous that "Midnight" (the title) is first explained in the... what... second-to-last chapter? I was incredibly confused when I read this book. <b>Why is this book named after a character that appears in the end of the book?</b> Yep. Yep, no one knows. :P<br /><br />If the world didn't suck, their journey through the wild would only take a few chapters. It wouldn't take the whole book. And sometimes I wish they weren't cats. That way, they could've stolen money and not have to stop by local ponds every two minutes. But the world sucks. <br /><br />Zzzzzzzzzzzzzz....... <span id="freeTextContainer14290439126628819661"> Hmmmmmmmm..... New main character, and what's this???? Switching off from other cats views?? Wow. Having this been the first time reading a book where different chapters had different view points from different characters, it was a little much to comprehend. However, it was a good read, with a new plot, and later in the future revealing that the next series would come together to make the best plot eva!!!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2859447305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2859447305" />
    <a title="GuineaPigFalconer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73657087-guineapigfalconer"><img alt="GuineaPigFalconer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510344418p2/73657087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2859447305?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="GuineaPigFalconer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="GuineaPigFalconer" href="/user/show/73657087-guineapigfalconer">GuineaPigFalconer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2859447305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1357010893790792828">I finished this book super quickly, in only a few days. It was nice to get back into the shorter Warriors series books after reading several super editions. This book starts off the second series, and I was quickly swept up into the new trouble facing the clan cats. The plot was fast-paced, the characters were good and grew throughout the book, and I look forward to getting further into this second Warriors series!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/90599773-erin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3405239617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12834103530220350266">This book was a perfect start to the next Warriors arc! A lot of new characters were introduced to shift the focus slightly onto this younger group while still having a lot of the original series cats involved, and I loved seeing both these generations interact. This was also one of Warriors stronger journey books, which I think is largely because we get to spend the first third of the book still in the forest and then still get glimpses of forest life throughout the rest of the book from Leafpa</span>
  <span id="freeText12834103530220350266" style="display:none">This book was a perfect start to the next Warriors arc! A lot of new characters were introduced to shift the focus slightly onto this younger group while still having a lot of the original series cats involved, and I loved seeing both these generations interact. This was also one of Warriors stronger journey books, which I think is largely because we get to spend the first third of the book still in the forest and then still get glimpses of forest life throughout the rest of the book from Leafpaw. I absolutely recommend this book and this arc as much as the original arc!</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3373420302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7809567014850295341">I had high hopes for this book, but I found that I was actually really disappointed as I kept reading it. The whole thing was basically about the 6 cats journeying, but it was so slow. I found myself drifting off in the middle of a sentence, then having to reread it all over again. So this wasn't the best book. I really hope that the next book in the series is better, but after this first one, I'm not really super excited.<br/>Hope you enjoy this book more than I did.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_6838961'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6838961-lone-wolf"><img alt="Lone Wolf (Wolves of the Beyond, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1328838824l/6838961._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mudePIO8VHSthrYzzxqJTWUlwez95oWXyhWl6OPN8mqkVpX2THLm3Q0tmYKGorEu+mwsRDcmNasDBMV5IrjIRg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8BLXUxSwf3Mm/CWMfn4ULmX0OkWjdasgzPjhK8UmdQrOoxyZ237N2oZXCj03xixN+r3X7Wm1GxwF6YG6BFNPJg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText9799551426073486612" style="display:none">Erin Hunter is the pseudonym of five people: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/132369.Kate_Cary" title="Kate Cary" rel="nofollow noopener">Kate Cary</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/220345.Cherith_Baldry" title="Cherith Baldry" rel="nofollow noopener">Cherith Baldry</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/374504.Tui_T__Sutherland" title="Tui T. Sutherland" rel="nofollow noopener">Tui T. Sutherland</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2742182.Gillian_Philip" title="Gillian Philip" rel="nofollow noopener">Gillian Philip</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/769868.Inbali_Iserles" title="Inbali Iserles" rel="nofollow noopener">Inbali Iserles</a>, as well as editor <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/645010.Victoria_Holmes" title="Victoria Holmes" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Holmes</a>. Together, they write the Warriors series as well as the Seekers and Survivors series. Erin Hunter is working on a new series now called Bravelands. <br /><br />Erin Hunter is inspired by a love of cats and a fascination with the ferocity of the natural world. As well as having a great respect for nature in all its forms, Erin enjoys creating rich mythical explanations for animal behavior, shaped by her interest in astronomy and standing stones.</span>

    first = d.getElementsByTagName('SCRIPT')[0],
    n = load.length,
    i = 0,
    go = function () {
      for (i = 0; i < n; i += 1) {

        script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);

    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
